                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رُوحٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">soul, spirit,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vital principle;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسٌ</foreign>; (IAar, IAmb, L, Msb, TA, and S and K &amp;c. in art. <foreign lang="ar">نفس</foreign>; [but there is a difference between these two words, for they are not always interchangeable, as I have shown in art. <foreign lang="ar">نفس</foreign>;]) [i. e.] <foreign lang="ar">مَا بِهِ حَيَاةُ الأَنْفُسِ</foreign>; (K; [see also <foreign lang="ar">رَوْحٌ</foreign>, third sentence;]) often occurring in the Kur and the Traditions in different senses, but generally signifying [as explained above, i. e.] the vital principle; (IAth, TA;) [or the <hi rend="ital">nervous fluid;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">animal spirit;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a subtile vaporous substance, which is the principle of vitality and of sensation and of voluntary motion;</hi> also called the <foreign lang="ar">رُوح حَيَوَانِىّ</foreign>; (KT in explanation of the term <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسٌ</foreign>;) or <hi rend="ital">a subtile body, the source of which is the hollow of the corporeal heart, and which diffuses itself into all the other parts of the body by means of the pulsing veins,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">arteries:</hi> (KT in explanation of the term <foreign lang="ar">الرُّوحُ الحَيَوَانِىُّ</foreign>: [so too <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسٌ</foreign>; q. v.: see also Gen. ix. 4: many of the ancients believed the soul to reside in the blood: see Aristotle, De Anim. i. 2, and Virgil's Æn. ix. 349:]) or the <hi rend="ital">vital principle in man:</hi> (Fr, TA:) or the <hi rend="ital">breath which a man breathes, and which pervades the whole body:</hi> [and this seems to be the original idea expressed by the word:] <hi rend="ital">after its exit, he ceases to breathe; and when it has completely gone forth, his eyes remain gazing towards it until they close; called in Pers.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جَانْ</foreign>: (AHeyth, TA:) accord. to the Sunnees, the <hi rend="ital">rational soul,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">النَّفْسُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّاطِقَةُ</foreign>, [also termed <foreign lang="ar">الرُّوحُ الإِنْسَانِىُّ</foreign>,]) <hi rend="ital">which is adapted to the faculty of making known its ideas by means of speech, and of understanding speech, and which perishes not with the perishing of the body, being a substance, not an accident;</hi> as is shown by the words in the Kur iii. 163, which refer to the <foreign lang="ar">روح</foreign>: (Msb:) most of the doctors of the fundamentals of religion forbid the diving into this matter, because God has abstained from making it known: (TA:) the philosophers say that it is the <hi rend="ital">blood, by the exhausting of which the life ceases:</hi> (Msb:) the word is masc., (IAar, IAmb, Az, S, M, A, Msb, K, *) thus, with the Arabs, differing from <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسٌ</foreign>, for this they make fem., (IAar, IAmb, Msb,) but the former is also fem., (S, M, A, Msb, K,) app. as meaning <foreign lang="ar">نَفْسٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) as is said in the R; (TA;) and most hold it to be as often fem. as it is masc.: (MF:) one says <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَ رُوحُهُ</foreign> (IAar, Az, TA) [and also <foreign lang="ar">خَرَجَتْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رُوحُهُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">His soul departed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">went forth</hi>]: the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَرْوَاحٌ</foreign>. (S, Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَفْخٌ</foreign> (K) [properly <hi rend="ital">A blowing</hi> with the mouth; but here] meaning <hi rend="ital">wind that issues from the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رُوح</foreign>; (TA;) <hi rend="ital">wind,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">breath.</hi> (ADk, TA.) Dhu-r-Rummeh says, respecting fire that he had struck, and upon which he bade his companion to blow, <foreign lang="ar">أَحْيِهَا بِرُوحِكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Give life to it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">enliven it, with thy wind</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">breath</hi>]. (TA.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">مَلَأَ القِرْبَةَ مِنْ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">He filled the skin with his wind; with his breath.</hi> (ADk, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">الرُّوحُ</foreign> also signifies <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Inspiration,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">divine revelation;</hi> (Zj, Th, K;) <hi rend="ital">such as is imparted by means of an angel:</hi> thus in the Kur xvi. 2 and xl. 15: so called because it quickens from the death of infidelity, and thus is, to a man, like the <foreign lang="ar">رُوح</foreign> which is the vital principle of his body: (T:) or (so says Zj accord. to the L, but in the K “ and ” ) <hi rend="ital">the prophetic commission.</hi> (Zj, K.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The Kur-án;</hi> (IAar, Zj, S, * A, * K;) whereby God's creatures are [spiritually] quickened, and guided to the right way.       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n16988-3" target="رُوَيْحَةٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n17004"/></foreign>. (T, Msb.) <foreign lang="ar">رِيَاحٌ</foreign>, or another form of pl., is often used in a good sense; and the sing., in an evil sense; because the Arabs say that the clouds are not made to give rain save by diverse winds blowing together; and this distinction is observed in the Kur-án. (L.) Hence, it is related in a trad., that he [Mohammad] used to say, when wind rose, <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُمَّ ٱجْعَلْهَا رِيَاحًا وَ لَا تَجْعَلْهَا رِيحًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">O God, make it to be winds, and made it not to be a wind</hi>].
